<p><i><b>Dangerous Woman</b></i> is the third studio album by American singer <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a>, released by <a href="/wiki/Republic_Records" title="Republic Records">Republic Records</a> on May 20, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The album is the follow-up to her second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/My_Everything_(Ariana_Grande_album)" title="My Everything (Ariana Grande album)">My Everything</a></i> (2014), and features guest appearances from <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macy_Gray" title="Macy Gray">Macy Gray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>. The album was originally to be titled <i>Moonlight</i> and the song "<a href="/wiki/Focus_(song)" title="Focus (song)">Focus</a>" was the intended lead single. However, later the album's name was changed to <i>Dangerous Woman</i> and "Focus" was removed from the album's standard track listing. <i>Dangerous Woman</i> is primarily a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> album, with influences of <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>. Grande, <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Savan_Kotecha" title="Savan Kotecha">Savan Kotecha</a> were the album's executive producers. All three wrote or produced songs for the album, as did musicians such as <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Salmanzadeh" title="Ilya Salmanzadeh">Ilya Salmanzadeh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Brown_(record_producer)" title="Tommy Brown (record producer)">Tommy Brown</a>.</p>
<p>The album debuted at number two on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, earning 175,000 <a href="/wiki/Album-equivalent_unit" title="Album-equivalent unit">album-equivalent units</a> in its first week, with 129,000 coming from pure sales. It was her first album to not hit number-one in the country. However, it became her first number one album in the UK. It also hit number-one in Australia, Brazil, Italy, Ireland, New Zealand, Spain and Taiwan, while also entering the top ten in almost every territory it charted in. The lead single "<a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Woman_(song)" title="Dangerous Woman (song)">Dangerous Woman</a>" was released on March 11, 2016, and peaked at number eight on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. The second and third singles, "<a href="/wiki/Into_You_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Into You (Ariana Grande song)">Into You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Side_to_Side" title="Side to Side">Side to Side</a>", have both reached peaks at numbers thirteen and four on that chart, respectively. Three promotional singles were released for the album: "<a href="/wiki/Be_Alright_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Be Alright (Ariana Grande song)">Be Alright</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Love_You_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Let Me Love You (Ariana Grande song)">Let Me Love You</a>" (featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>), and "Jason's Song (Gave It Away)".</p>
<p>The album received generally positive reviews from critics, appearing on the year-end lists of many publications and has received a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Best Pop Vocal Album</a>. To promote the album, Grande performed at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2016 Billboard Music Awards">2016 <i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2016 MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2016" title="American Music Awards of 2016">American Music Awards</a>. She also appeared on an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> as both the host and musical guest. Furthermore, Grande intends to embark on a concert tour, the <a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Woman_Tour" title="Dangerous Woman Tour">Dangerous Woman Tour</a>, in 2017.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Grande began recording songs for the album soon after the completion of her previous album, <i><a href="/wiki/My_Everything_(Ariana_Grande_album)" title="My Everything (Ariana Grande album)">My Everything</a></i> (2014), and continued throughout the summer and fall of 2015, between stops on her <a href="/wiki/The_Honeymoon_Tour" title="The Honeymoon Tour">Honeymoon Tour</a>, with her friends <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Brown_(record_producer)" title="Tommy Brown (record producer)">Tommy Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Mon%C3%A9t" title="Victoria Monét">Victoria Monét</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Focus_(song)" title="Focus (song)">Focus</a>", which was originally intended to be the lead single from the album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> was released digitally on October 30, 2015. The song debuted and peaked at number seven on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> selling 113,000 copies in its first week in the United States. Grande finished work on the album on January 21, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album was originally to be titled <i>Moonlight</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> On <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live!</a></i> in January 2016, however, Grande revealed that she was no longer sure of the name, and that she might re-title the album after another song on the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> She announced the new title of the album, <i>Dangerous Woman</i>, on February 22, 2016, through her <a href="/wiki/Snapchat" title="Snapchat">Snapchat</a> and Twitter accounts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The following day, she posted a photo on Instagram with a caption quoting Egyptian feminist writer <a href="/wiki/Nawal_El_Saadawi" title="Nawal El Saadawi">Nawal El Saadawi</a>'s 1975 novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Woman_at_Point_Zero" title="Woman at Point Zero">Woman at Point Zero</a></i> as follows: "They said, 'You are a savage and dangerous woman.' I am speaking the truth. And the truth is savage and dangerous".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> As to why the album name was changed, Grande stated that it had to do with portraying herself as a stronger person and to empower fans, saying: "'Moonlight' is a lovely song, and it's a lovely title. It's really romantic, and it definitely ties together the old music and the new music, but 'Dangerous Woman' is a lot stronger. ... To me, a dangerous woman is someone who's not afraid to take a stand, be herself and to be honest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Grande announced the final title of the album on February 22, 2016, via her Snapchat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Two days later, Grande launched a website to promote her album (now merged with her original website), which features a "Tea" section in which the singer shares new information regarding the album, as well as a "Shop" section, in which album-related merchandise is sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The official album cover was released on March 10 via Grande's social media accounts and on her official website. On March 12, 2016, Grande was both the host and musical guest on NBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, where she performed "<a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Woman_(song)" title="Dangerous Woman (song)">Dangerous Woman</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Be_Alright_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Be Alright (Ariana Grande song)">Be Alright</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In April, Grande debuted "Leave Me Lonely" live at the grand opening of the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a> <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_Arena" title="T-Mobile Arena">T-Mobile Arena</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> and performed at the <a href="/wiki/2016_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2016 MTV Movie Awards">2016 MTV Movie Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> On May 13, 2016, Grande announced via her Instagram account that a new song from the album would be premiered exclusively on <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a> every day until the release of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The songs released, in order of release, were "Everyday" featuring <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, "Greedy", "Side to Side", featuring <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, "Sometimes", "Leave Me Lonely", featuring <a href="/wiki/Macy_Gray" title="Macy Gray">Macy Gray</a>, "Touch It", and "Bad Decisions". Grande promoted the album's release with televised performances at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2016 Billboard Music Awards">2016 <i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and on <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live!</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> On May 25, she sang "<a href="/wiki/Into_You_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Into You (Ariana Grande song)">Into You</a>" and duetted with <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a> on "Dangerous Woman" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Voice_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The Voice (U.S. TV series)">The Voice</a></i> season 10 finale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Summertime_Ball" title="Summertime Ball">Summertime Ball</a> at London's <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> in June, Grande performed "Dangerous Woman, "Into You", and "Greedy" from the album as part of her set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Grande later performed at the <a href="/wiki/2016_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2016 MTV Video Music Awards">2016 MTV Video Music Awards</a> with Minaj to promote the album's third single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> She also appeared on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show with Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show with Jimmy Fallon</a></i> on September 8, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2016" title="American Music Awards of 2016">American Music Awards</a> on November 20, 2016, where she performed "Side to Side" alongside Minaj and won 'Artist of the Year' later in the evening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tour">Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Woman_Tour" title="Dangerous Woman Tour">Dangerous Woman Tour</a></div>
<p>Grande first announced plans to tour on the <i>Dangerous Woman</i> website in May 2016. On September 9, 2016, Grande announced the dates for the first leg of the <a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Woman_Tour" title="Dangerous Woman Tour">Dangerous Woman Tour</a>, with ticket pre-sales beginning on September 20, 2016 and tickets going on general sale on September 24, 2016. The tour is set to begin on February 2, 2017 in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Grande's song "<a href="/wiki/Focus_(song)" title="Focus (song)">Focus</a>", was released on October 30, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Although originally intended to be the lead single, it was not included on the standard or deluxe editions of <i>Dangerous Woman</i>. However, it was included as a bonus track on the Japanese edition of the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JPA_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-JPA-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> "Focus" was certified platinum by the RIAA<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAcert_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAcert-31">[31]</a></sup> and had sold 425,000 copies in the US as of May 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">

<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>

<p>The album's lead single and title track, "<a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Woman_(song)" title="Dangerous Woman (song)">Dangerous Woman</a>", was teased by Grande on March 1, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> A snippet of the song was released as background music to the <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret_Swim_Special" title="Victoria's Secret Swim Special">Victoria's Secret Swim Special</a> on March 9, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The single was released on March 11, 2016, along with the pre-order of the album on the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fuseguide_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-fuseguide-35">[35]</a></sup> The track earned 118,000 digital downloads in its opening week and debuted at number ten on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, becoming Grande's seventh Hot 100 top ten and fifth to debut in the top ten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billde_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billde-36">[36]</a></sup> The single made Grande the first artist in the chart's 57-year history to debut in the top 10 with the lead single from each of her first three albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billde_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billde-36">[36]</a></sup> The single was later sent to radio on March 15, 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and reached a new peak of number 8 in its eleventh week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> On June 2016, "Dangerous Woman" was certified platinum by the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAAcert_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-RIAAcert-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Into_You_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Into You (Ariana Grande song)">Into You</a>", was released on May 6, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> It was sent to radio stations on June 28, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top40rhythmic_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-top40rhythmic-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-top40_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-top40-41">[41]</a></sup> The song debuted at number 83 and reached a peak of number 13 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Side_to_Side" title="Side to Side">Side to Side</a>", featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, was released on August 30, 2016 as the album's third single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allaccesssidetoside_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-allaccesssidetoside-43">[43]</a></sup> It debuted at number 31 and peaked at number 4 on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Internationally, it has reached number two in Bulgaria and New Zealand, number three in Australia, number four in UK, number five in Ireland, as well as the top 40 in several other countries, such as Canada and The Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Everyday_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Everyday (Ariana Grande song)">Everyday</a>", featuring rapper <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a>, was released on January 10, 2017 as the album's fourth single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotional_singles">Promotional singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Promotional singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first promotional single, "<a href="/wiki/Be_Alright_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Be Alright (Ariana Grande song)">Be Alright</a>", was released on March 18, 2016. The song debuted and peaked at number 43 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Be_Alright_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Be_Alright-48">[48]</a></sup> The second promotional single, "<a href="/wiki/Let_Me_Love_You_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Let Me Love You (Ariana Grande song)">Let Me Love You</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, was released on April 18, 2016 debuting and peaking at number 99 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-digitalspy1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-digitalspy1-49">[49]</a></sup> The third promotional single, "Jason's Song (Gave It Away)" was released on September 16, 2016.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle">6/10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spin_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-spin-61">[61]</a></sup></td>

</table>
<p><i>Dangerous Woman</i> received generally positive reviews from music critics. According to <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Weighted_arithmetic_mean" title="Weighted arithmetic mean">weighted average</a> score out of 100 to ratings and reviews from mainstream critics, critics gave <i>Dangerous Woman</i> a score of 76, based on 14 reviews, indicating "generally favorable reviews".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metacriticrv_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Metacriticrv-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> wrote for <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> that "track by track, <i>Dangerous Woman</i> has sly, subtle distinctions – a little bit of torch gives way to some heavy hip only to have frothy pop surface again", and that "while some of these cuts work better than others, the range is impressive, as is Grande's measured, assured performance."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllMusic_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusic-52">[52]</a></sup> In his review for <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, Nolan Feeney commented that while Grande's previous album, '<a href="/wiki/My_Everything_(Ariana_Grande_album)" title="My Everything (Ariana Grande album)">My Everything</a>', "suffered for trying to be everything", on <i>Dangerous Woman</i>, "with a streamlined team of hitmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a>, she pulls off pop, R&amp;B, reggae, and house—all without overextending herself or pandering to trends".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-ew-54">[54]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i>'s Annie Zaleski agreed, stating that the album "possesses more personality than 'My Everything'," and writes in conclusion that "'Dangerous Woman' is an effortless leap forward on which Grande comes into her own as a vocalist and performer."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-avclub-53">[53]</a></sup> Lewis Corner from <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a> noted that Grande "ultimately pulled together a consistent collection that impressively manages to keep your attention over 15 tracks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DigitalSpy_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-DigitalSpy-62">[62]</a></sup> Mikael Wood, writing for the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, found it "impressive how fully she inhabits the emotional environment of each song" on the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LosAngelesTimes_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-LosAngelesTimes-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The song was considered the most unsatisfying collaboration from the album by <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Future_(rapper)" title="Future (rapper)">Future</a> repeating the song’s title, making him <i>Dangerous Woman'</i>s more minimalist version of <a href="/wiki/Big_Sean" title="Big Sean">Big Sean</a> on "<a href="/wiki/Problem_(Ariana_Grande_song)" title="Problem (Ariana Grande song)">Problem</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pitchfork_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork-57">[57]</a></sup></div>

</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Larry Bartleet of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> wrote that apart from the "consistent songwriting clout that elevates this album from recent efforts by Grande's teen-star peers, <a href="/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a> and <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>", the "modish message of empowerment feels honest coming from Grande."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NME_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-NME-55">[55]</a></sup> Michael Cragg from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> noted that during her successful previous album she had lost her identity in the process, but in comparison, he noted that the album is a "refinement of her sound", and concluded that "held together by Grande's skyscraping voice, <i>Dangerous Woman</i> throws a lot at the wall and, brilliantly, most of it sticks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observer_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-observer-56">[56]</a></sup> Erik Ernst of <i><a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Journal_Sentinel" title="Milwaukee Journal Sentinel">Milwaukee Journal Sentinel</a></i> opined that "like much of the disc, it's an unexpected, but remarkable, choice from a confident pop star ready to set her own path to the top."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MilwaukeeJournalSentinel_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-MilwaukeeJournalSentinel-64">[64]</a></sup> Maeve McDermott of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> summarized that <i>Dangerous Woman</i>, "like its title suggests", is "a mature portrait of an artist blessed with one of pop's strongest voices, brimming with potential hits."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAToday_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAToday-65">[65]</a></sup> Quinn Moreland of <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_(website)" title="Pitchfork (website)">Pitchfork</a> viewed that "Grande does not need to force any sort of spirit, she is full of it already. She just needs to find the Dangerous Woman within herself and let her break free."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pitchfork_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-Pitchfork-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Plain_Dealer" title="The Plain Dealer">The Plain Dealer</a></i>'s Troy L. Smith wrote that the album "plays it safe and smart", explaining it "functions as 'My Everything 2.0' – a collection of pitch-perfect hooks and slick production built in the mold of Mariah Carey."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cleveland_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland-66">[66]</a></sup> For Theon Weber of <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i>, "Grande is most complete on record when she's playing a diva."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spin_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-spin-61">[61]</a></sup> Sal Cinquemani of <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a> wrote that Grande "too often tries to look and sound more mature than she is,"observing that "the songs on the album's latter half are limited by their strict adherence to contemporary pop and R&amp;B trends."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slant_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-slant-59">[59]</a></sup> In a mixed review, Christopher R. Weingarten of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> opined that "as an album artist, she's prone to a schizophrenic sound and unfortunate sequencing," adding that "we're still no closer to figuring out who she wants to be." He also said that "her talents are wasted on meaningful-sounding but ultimately trite lyrics. However, her phrasing remains unique and powerful and pyrotechnic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone-58">[58]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the United States, <i>Dangerous Woman</i> debuted at number 2 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Views_(album)" title="Views (album)">Views</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>. It earned 175,000 <a href="/wiki/Album-equivalent_unit" title="Album-equivalent unit">album-equivalent units</a>, with 129,000 coming from pure album sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In the second week, the album dropped to number 6, selling 50,000 equivalent units,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> while in the third week, it slipped to number 7, with 33,000 equivalent units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On October 28, 2016, <i>Dangerous Woman</i> was certified Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a> for combined album sales, on-demand audio, video streams and track-sale equivalent of 1 million units. As of January 1, 2017, the album has moved 1,032,000 units in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Japan, the album debuted at number 2 on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon_Albums_Chart" title="Oricon Albums Chart">Oricon Albums Chart</a>, selling 20,811 copies in its opening week, and becoming Grande's highest album ranking in that region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In the second week, the album dropped to number 8, selling 11,950 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In the third week, it stayed at number 8, with 7,022 copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> As of June 2016, <i>Dangerous Woman</i> has sold 50,000 copies in Japan. In September, it was certified Gold for shipments of 125,000 copies in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, the album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">Official Albums Chart</a>, becoming Grande's first number one album in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The album also reached the top of the charts in several other markets, including Australia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aria_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-aria-84">[84]</a></sup> Brazil,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-br_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-br-85">[85]</a></sup> Ireland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ie_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-ie-86">[86]</a></sup> Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-italy_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-italy-87">[87]</a></sup> Netherlands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dutch_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-dutch-88">[88]</a></sup> New Zealand,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nz_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-nz-89">[89]</a></sup> Norway,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nor_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-nor-90">[90]</a></sup> Spain<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spain_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-spain-91">[91]</a></sup> and Taiwan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taiwan_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-taiwan-92">[92]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_formats">Release formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dangerous_Woman_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
